<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">This article is about Genghis Khan, the historical figure and Mongol leader. <p><b>Genghis Khan</b><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[note 3]</a></sup> (born <b>Temüjin</b>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Temujin_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-Temujin-2">[note 1]</a></sup> <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 1162</span> – August 25, 1227)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ter92_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-Ter92-3">[2]</a></sup> was the founder and first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_Khan" title="Great Khan">Great Khan</a> (<a href="/wiki/Emperor" title="Emperor">Emperor</a>) of the <a href="/wiki/Mongol_Empire" title="Mongol Empire">Mongol Empire</a>, which became the <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_empires" title="List of largest empires">largest contiguous empire</a> in history after his death. He came to power by uniting many of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nomadic_tribe" title="Nomadic tribe">nomadic tribes</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mongol_steppe" title="Mongol steppe">Mongol steppe</a> and being proclaimed the universal <a href="/wiki/List_of_Mongol_rulers" title="List of Mongol rulers">ruler of the Mongols</a>, or <i>Genghis Khan</i>. With the tribes of <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Asia" title="Northeast Asia">Northeast Asia</a> largely under his control, he set in motion the <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasions_and_conquests" title="Mongol invasions and conquests">Mongol invasions</a>, which ultimately witnessed the conquest of much of <a href="/wiki/Eurasia" title="Eurasia">Eurasia</a>, and incursions by Mongol raiding parties as far west as <a href="/wiki/Legnica" title="Legnica">Legnica</a> in <a href="/wiki/Mongol_Empire#Push_into_central_Europe" title="Mongol Empire">western Poland</a> and as far south as <a href="/wiki/Gaza_City" title="Gaza City">Gaza</a>. He launched campaigns against the <a href="/wiki/Mongol_conquest_of_the_Qara_Khitai" title="Mongol conquest of the Qara Khitai">Qara Khitai</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mongol_conquest_of_the_Khwarazmian_Empire" title="Mongol conquest of the Khwarazmian Empire">Khwarezmia</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Mongol_conquest_of_Western_Xia" title="Mongol conquest of Western Xia">Western Xia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mongol_conquest_of_the_Jin_dynasty" title="Mongol conquest of the Jin dynasty">Jin dynasty</a> during his life, and his generals raided into <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasions_of_Georgia" title="Mongol invasions of Georgia">medieval Georgia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasion_of_Circassia" title="Mongol invasion of Circassia">Circassia</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasion_of_Kievan_Rus%27" title="Mongol invasion of Kievan Rus'">Kievan Rus'</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasion_of_Volga_Bulgaria" title="Mongol invasion of Volga Bulgaria">Volga Bulgaria</a>.
</p><p>His exceptional military successes made Genghis Khan one of the most important conquerors of all time, and by the end of the Great Khan's life, the Mongol Empire occupied a substantial portion of <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Song_dynasty" title="Song dynasty">China</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[10]</a></sup> Genghis Khan and his story of conquest have a fearsome reputation in local histories.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mongolia_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-mongolia-14">[11]</a></sup> Many medieval chroniclers and modern historians describe Genghis Khan's conquests as wholesale <a href="/wiki/Destruction_under_the_Mongol_Empire" title="Destruction under the Mongol Empire">destruction on an unprecedented scale</a> that led to drastic population declines in some regions as a result of both <a href="/wiki/Mass_murder" title="Mass murder">mass exterminations</a> and <a href="/wiki/Famine" title="Famine">famine</a>. Estimates of the number of people who died as a consequence of Genghis Khan's military campaigns range from about four million in the most conservative estimates to up to sixty million in the most sweeping historical accounts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELane200429–41_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELane200429–41-15">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[14]</a></sup> On the other hand, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buddhist" title="Buddhist">Buddhist</a> <a href="/wiki/Uyghur_Khaganate#Successors" title="Uyghur Khaganate">Uyghur</a> kingdom of <a href="/wiki/Qocho" title="Qocho">Qocho</a>, for example, viewed him as a liberator and voluntarily left the Qara Khitai empire to become <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mongol" title="Mongol">Mongol</a> <a href="/wiki/Vassal_state" title="Vassal state">vassals</a>. Genghis Khan was also portrayed beneficently by early <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">Renaissance</a> sources out of respect for the great spread of culture, technology and ideas along the <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road" title="Silk Road">Silk Road</a> under the Mongol Empire.<sup class="reference" id='cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeatherford2005[[Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_August_2021]]&lt;sup_class="noprint_Inline-Template_"_style="white-space:nowrap;"&gt;&amp;#91;&lt;i&gt;[[Wikipedia:Citing_sources|&lt;span_title="This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears.&amp;#32;(August_2021)"&gt;page&amp;nbsp;needed&lt;/span&gt;]]&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#93;&lt;/sup&gt;_18-0'><a href='#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeatherford2005[[Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_August_2021]]&lt;sup_class="noprint_Inline-Template_"_style="white-space:nowrap;"&gt;&amp;#91;&lt;i&gt;[[Wikipedia:Citing_sources|&lt;span_title="This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears.&amp;#32;(August_2021)"&gt;page&amp;nbsp;needed&lt;/span&gt;]]&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#93;&lt;/sup&gt;-18'>[15]</a></sup>
</p><p>Beyond his military successes, Genghis Khan's civil achievements included the establishment of <a href="/wiki/Yassa" title="Yassa">Mongol law</a> and the adoption of the <a href="/wiki/Old_Uyghur_alphabet" title="Old Uyghur alphabet">Uyghur script</a> as a writing system across his vast territories. He also practiced <a href="/wiki/Meritocracy" title="Meritocracy">meritocracy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Religious_tolerance" title="Religious tolerance">religious tolerance</a>. Present-day <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mongolians" title="Mongolians">Mongolians</a> regard him as the founding father of <a href="/wiki/Mongolia" title="Mongolia">Mongolia</a> for unifying the nomadic tribes of Northeast Asia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[16]</a></sup> By bringing the <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road" title="Silk Road">Silk Road</a> under one cohesive political environment, he also considerably eased communication and trade between Northeast Asia, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">Muslim</a> Southwest Asia, and Christian <a href="/wiki/Europe#High_and_Late_Middle_Ages" title="Europe">Europe</a>, boosting global commerce and expanding the cultural horizons of all the Eurasian civilizations of the day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[17]</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Name_and_spelling">Name and spelling</span></h2>
<p>According to the <i>Secret History</i>, Genghis Khan's birth name <i>Temüjin</i> (<a href="/wiki/Simplified_Chinese_characters" title="Simplified Chinese characters">simplified Chinese</a>: <span lang="zh-Hans"><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E9%93%81%E6%9C%A8%E7%9C%9F" title="wikt:铁木真">铁木真</a></span>; <a href="/wiki/Traditional_Chinese_characters" title="Traditional Chinese characters">traditional Chinese</a>: <span lang="zh-Hant"><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E9%90%B5%E6%9C%A8%E7%9C%9E" title="wikt:鐵木眞">鐵木眞</a></span>; <a href="/wiki/Pinyin" title="Pinyin">pinyin</a>: <i><span lang="zh-Latn-pinyin">Tiěmùzhēn</span></i>) came from the <a href="/wiki/Tatars" title="Tatars">Tatar</a> chief Temüjin-üge whom his father had just captured. The name Temüjin is also equated with the Turco-Mongol <i>temürči(n)</i>, "<a href="/wiki/Blacksmith" title="Blacksmith">blacksmith</a>", and there existed a tradition that viewed Genghis Khan as a smith, according to <a href="/wiki/Paul_Pelliot" title="Paul Pelliot">Paul Pelliot</a>, which, though unfounded, was well established by the middle of the 13th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[18]</a></sup>
</p><p><i>Genghis Khan</i> is an honorary title meaning "universal ruler" that represents an aggrandization of the pre-existing title of <i>Khan</i> that is used to denote a clan chief in Mongolian. The appellation of "Genghis" to the term is thought to derive from the <a href="/wiki/Turkic_languages" title="Turkic languages">Turkic</a> word "<i>tengiz</i>", meaning <a href="/wiki/Sea" title="Sea">sea</a>, making the honorary title literally "oceanic ruler", but understood more broadly as a metaphor for the universality or totality of Temüjin's rule from a Mongol perspective.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BRE_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-BRE-23">[20]</a></sup> Genghis Khan is spelled in a variety of ways in different languages such as <a href="/wiki/Mongolian_language" title="Mongolian language">Mongolian</a> <i>Chinggis Khaan</i>, English <i>Chinghiz</i>, <i>Chinghis</i>, and <i>Chingiz</i>; <a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">Chinese</a>: <span lang="zh"><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E6%88%90%E5%90%89%E6%80%9D%E6%B1%97" title="wikt:成吉思汗">成吉思汗</a></span>; <a href="/wiki/Pinyin" title="Pinyin">pinyin</a>: <i><span lang="zh-Latn-pinyin">Chéngjísī Hán</span></i>; <a href="/wiki/Turkic_languages" title="Turkic languages">Turkic</a>: <i>Cengiz Han</i>, <i>Çingiz Xan</i>, <i>Chingizxon</i>, <i>Shın'g'ısxan</i>, <i>Çingiz Han</i>, <i>Çıñğız Xan</i>, <i>Şıñğıs xan</i>, <i>Çiñğiz Xaan</i>, <i>Çiñğizhan</i>; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_languages" title="Russian languages">Russian</a>: <span title="Russian-language text"><span lang="ru">Чингисхан</span></span> (<i>Čingiskhan</i>) or <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%D0%A7%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B3%D0%B8%D0%B7-%D1%85%D0%B0%D0%BD" title="wikt:Чингиз-хан">Чингиз-хан</a> (<i>Čingiz-khan</i>), <a href="/wiki/Hindi" title="Hindi">Hindi</a>: चङ्ग़ेज़ ख़ान (<i>Caṅġēz Ḵẖān</i>), <a href="/wiki/Punjabi_language" title="Punjabi language">Punjabi</a>: ਚੰਗ਼ੀਜ਼ ਖ਼ਾਨ, چنغیز خان (<i>Caṅġīz Ḵẖān</i>), <a href="/wiki/Urdu" title="Urdu">Urdu</a>: چنغیز خان (<i>Caṅġīz Ḵẖān</i>), <a href="/wiki/Persian_language" title="Persian language">Persian</a>: چنگیز خان (<i>Čəngīz H̱ān</i>), <a href="/wiki/Arabic" title="Arabic">Arabic</a>: چنغیز خان (<i>Cənġīz H̱ān</i>).
</p><p>When <a href="/wiki/Kublai_Khan" title="Kublai Khan">Kublai Khan</a> established the <a href="/wiki/Yuan_dynasty" title="Yuan dynasty">Yuan dynasty</a> in 1271, he had his grandfather Genghis Khan placed in official records and accorded him the <a href="/wiki/Temple_name" title="Temple name">temple name</a> <i>Taizu</i> (<a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">Chinese</a>: <span lang="zh">太祖</span>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TempleName1_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-TempleName1-7">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TempleName2_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-TempleName2-8">[6]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Posthumous_name" title="Posthumous name">posthumous name</a> <i>Emperor Shengwu</i> (<a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">Chinese</a>: <span lang="zh">聖武皇帝</span>). Genghis Khan is thus also referred to as <i>Yuan Taizu</i> (Emperor Taizu of Yuan; <a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">Chinese</a>: <span lang="zh">元太祖</span>) in <a href="/wiki/Chinese_historiography" title="Chinese historiography">Chinese historiography</a>. <a href="/wiki/K%C3%BCl%C3%BCg_Khan" title="Külüg Khan">Külüg Khan</a> later expanded Genghis Khan's title to <i>Emperor Fatian Qiyun Shengwu</i> (<a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">Chinese</a>: <span lang="zh">法天啟運聖武皇帝</span>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PosthumousName_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-PosthumousName-6">[4]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lineage_and_birth">Lineage and birth</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Burkhan_Khaldun_mount3.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="471" data-file-width="709" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Burkhan_Khaldun_mount3.jpg/220px-Burkhan_Khaldun_mount3.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Burkhan_Khaldun_mount3.jpg/330px-Burkhan_Khaldun_mount3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Burkhan_Khaldun_mount3.jpg/440px-Burkhan_Khaldun_mount3.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Burkhan_Khaldun_mount3.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Burkhan Khaldun mountain</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Onon.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="960" data-file-width="1280" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Onon.jpg/220px-Onon.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Onon.jpg/330px-Onon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Onon.jpg/440px-Onon.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Onon.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Autumn at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Onon_River" title="Onon River">Onon River</a>, Mongolia, the region where Temüjin was born and grew up</div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Family_tree_of_Genghis_Khan" title="Family tree of Genghis Khan">Family tree of Genghis Khan</a></div>
<p>Temüjin was born the first son of <a href="/wiki/Hoelun" title="Hoelun">Hoelun</a>, second wife of his father <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yes%C3%BCgei" title="Yesügei">Yesügei</a>, who was the chief of the <a href="/wiki/Borjigin" title="Borjigin">Borjigin</a> clan in the nomadic <a href="/wiki/Khamag_Mongol" title="Khamag Mongol">Khamag Mongol</a> confederation,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BRE_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-BRE-23">[20]</a></sup> nephew to <a href="/wiki/Ambaghai" title="Ambaghai">Ambaghai</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hotula_Khan" title="Hotula Khan">Hotula Khan</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDerenkoMalyarchukaWozniakbDenisovaa20072_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDerenkoMalyarchukaWozniakbDenisovaa20072-24">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELee20164–6_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELee20164–6-25">[22]</a></sup> and an ally of <a href="/wiki/Toghrul" title="Toghrul">Toghrul</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Keraites" title="Keraites"> Keraite</a> tribe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMorgan198658_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMorgan198658-26">[23]</a></sup> Temüjin was related on his father's side to <a href="/wiki/Khabul_Khan" title="Khabul Khan">Khabul Khan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ambaghai" title="Ambaghai">Ambaghai</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hotula_Khan" title="Hotula Khan">Hotula Khan</a>, who had headed the <a href="/wiki/Khamag_Mongol" title="Khamag Mongol">Khamag Mongol</a> confederation and were descendants of <a href="/wiki/Bodonchar_Munkhag" title="Bodonchar Munkhag">Bodonchar Munkhag</a> (<abbr title="circa">c.</abbr> 900),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERatchnevsky19919–10_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERatchnevsky19919–10-27">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDerenkoMalyarchukaWozniakbDenisovaa20075_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDerenkoMalyarchukaWozniakbDenisovaa20075-28">[25]</a></sup> while his mother <a href="/wiki/Hoelun" title="Hoelun">Hoelun</a> was from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Olkhunut" title="Olkhunut">Olkhunut</a> sub-lineage of the <a href="/wiki/Khongirad" title="Khongirad">Khongirad</a> tribe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[27]</a></sup> Temüjin's noble background made it easier for him, later in life, to solicit help from and eventually consolidate the other Mongol tribes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEColumbia_University3_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEColumbia_University3-31">[28]</a></sup>
</p><p>There is considerable uncertainty surrounding both the date and location of Temüjin's birth, with historical accounts assigning dates of birth ranging from 1155 to 1182 and a wide variety of possible birth locations. The Arab historian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rashid-al-Din_Hamadani" title="Rashid-al-Din Hamadani">Rashid al-Din</a> asserted that Temüjin was born in 1155, while the <i><a href="/wiki/History_of_Yuan" title="History of Yuan">History of Yuan</a></i> records his year of birth as 1162 and Tibetan sources implausibly present 1182 as the correct date.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ter92_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-Ter92-3">[2]</a></sup> Modern historical studies have largely attested the 1162 date presented by the Chinese history as the most realistic, given the significant problems associated with how either the 1155 or 1182 dates would reflect on other event's in Temüjin's timeline.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERatchnevsky19919–10_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERatchnevsky19919–10-27">[24]</a></sup> Accepting a birth in 1155, for instance, would render Temüjin a father at the age of 30 and would imply that he personally commanded the expedition against the <a href="/wiki/Tangut_people" title="Tangut people">Tanguts</a> at the age of 72.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERatchnevsky19919–10_27-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERatchnevsky19919–10-27">[24]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Secret_History_of_the_Mongols" title="The Secret History of the Mongols">The Secret History of the Mongols</a></i> relates that Temüjin was an infant during the attack by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Merkits" title="Merkits">Merkits</a>, when a birth date of 1155 would have made him 18 years old.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERatchnevsky19919–10_27-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERatchnevsky19919–10-27">[24]</a></sup> The 1162 date has meanwhile been attested by various sources, including a 1992 study of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mongol_calendar" title="Mongol calendar">Mongol calendar</a> commissioned by <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> that suggested the specific date of 1 May 1162.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ter92_3-3"><a href="#cite_note-Ter92-3">[2]</a></sup>
</p><p>The location of Temüjin's birth largely shrouded in mystery, with a wide range of locations proposed, many in the vicinity of the mountain <a href="/wiki/Burkhan_Khaldun" title="Burkhan Khaldun">Burkhan Khaldun</a>. One such location is <a href="/wiki/Del%C3%BC%C3%BCn_Boldog" title="Delüün Boldog">Delüün Boldog</a>, which lies near the rivers <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Onon_River" title="Onon River">Onon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kherlen_River" title="Kherlen River">Kherlen</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERatchnevsky19919–10_27-4"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERatchnevsky19919–10-27">[24]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tribal_upbringing">Tribal upbringing</span></h3>
<p>Temüjin grew up with three brothers, <a href="/wiki/Qasar" title="Qasar">Qasar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hachiun" title="Hachiun">Hachiun</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tem%C3%BCge" title="Temüge">Temüge</a>; one sister, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tem%C3%BClen" title="Temülen">Temülen</a>; and two half-brothers, <a href="/wiki/Behter" title="Behter">Behter</a> and <a href="/wiki/Belgutei" title="Belgutei">Belgutei</a>. As was common to <a href="/wiki/Nomad" title="Nomad">nomads</a> in Mongolia, Temüjin's early life was marked by difficulties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELee20163_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELee20163-32">[29]</a></sup>
</p><p>At age nine, his father <a href="/wiki/Arranged_marriage" title="Arranged marriage">arranged a marriage</a> for him and delivered him to the family of his future wife <a href="/wiki/B%C3%B6rte" title="Börte">Börte</a> of the tribe <a href="/wiki/Khongirad" title="Khongirad">Khongirad</a>. Temüjin was to live there serving the head of the household Dai Setsen until the <a href="/wiki/Child_marriage" title="Child marriage">marriageable age</a> of 12.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERachewiltz20153_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERachewiltz20153-33">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAtwood2004a2_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAtwood2004a2-34">[31]</a></sup> While heading home, his father ran into the neighboring <a href="/wiki/Tatars" title="Tatars">Tatars</a>, who had long been Mongol enemies, and they offered his father food under the guise of hospitality, but instead poisoned him. Upon learning this, Temüjin returned home to claim his father's position as chief, but the tribe refused him and abandoned the family, leaving it without protection.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[32]</a></sup>
</p><p>For the next several years, the family lived in poverty, surviving mostly on wild fruits, ox <a href="/wiki/Carrion" title="Carrion">carcasses</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marmot" title="Marmot">marmots</a>, and other small game killed by Temüjin and his brothers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeatherford2005[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidA8Y9B5uHQcACpgPA23_23]_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeatherford2005[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidA8Y9B5uHQcACpgPA23_23]-36">[33]</a></sup> During this time, Temüjin's mother, Hoelun, taught him about Mongol politics, including the lack of unity between the different clans and the need for arranged marriages to solidify temporary alliances, and strong <a href="/wiki/Military_alliance" title="Military alliance">alliances</a> to ultimately ensure the stability of Mongolia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERachewiltz20155_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERachewiltz20155-37">[34]</a></sup> Indeed, he was later successful, in part, because of his mother's role as a warrior in battle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[35]</a></sup>
</p><p>Over time, Temüjin's older half-brother Behter began to exercise power as the eldest male in the family,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeatherford2005[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidA8Y9B5uHQcACpgPA23_23]_36-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeatherford2005[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidA8Y9B5uHQcACpgPA23_23]-36">[33]</a></sup> creating tension in the family that boiled over during one hunting excursion by the men of the family and resulted in the death of Behter at the hands of Temüjin and his brother Qasar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeatherford2005[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidA8Y9B5uHQcACpgPA23_23]_36-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeatherford2005[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidA8Y9B5uHQcACpgPA23_23]-36">[33]</a></sup>
</p><p>Later, in a raid around 1177, Temüjin was captured by his father's former allies, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tayichi%27ud" title="Tayichi'ud">Tayichi'ud</a>, enslaved, and, reportedly humiliated by being shacked in a <a href="/wiki/Cangue" title="Cangue">cangue</a> (a form of portable stocks). With the help of a sympathetic guard, he escaped from the <a href="/wiki/Yurt" title="Yurt">ger</a> (yurt) at night by hiding in a river crevice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAtwood2004a5_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAtwood2004a5-39">[36]</a></sup> The escape earned Temüjin a reputation. Soon, <a href="/wiki/Jelme" title="Jelme">Jelme</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bo%27orchu" title="Bo'orchu">Bo'orchu</a> joined forces with him, and they and the guard's son <a href="/wiki/Chilaun" title="Chilaun">Chilaun</a> eventually became generals of Genghis Khan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERachewiltz20157_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERachewiltz20157-40">[37]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wives_and_concubines">Wives and concubines</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wives_of_Genghis_Khan" title="Wives of Genghis Khan">Wives of Genghis Khan</a></div>
<p>As was common for powerful Mongol men, Temüjin had many wives and concubines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcLynn2015[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidjcQzCgAAQBAJpgPA169_169]_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcLynn2015[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidjcQzCgAAQBAJpgPA169_169]-41">[38]</a></sup> These women were often queens or princesses that were taken captive from the territories he conquered or gifted to him by allies, vassals, or other tribal acquaintances.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBroadbridge201874,_92_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBroadbridge201874,_92-42">[39]</a></sup> His principal or most famous wives and concubines included: <a href="/wiki/B%C3%B6rte" title="Börte">Börte</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yesugen" title="Yesugen">Yesugen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yesui" title="Yesui">Yesui</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Khulan_Khatun&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Khulan Khatun (page does not exist)">Khulan Khatun</a>, <a href="/wiki/M%C3%B6ge_Khatun" title="Möge Khatun">Möge Khatun</a>, <a href="/wiki/Juerbiesu" title="Juerbiesu">Juerbiesu</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ibaqa_Beki" title="Ibaqa Beki">Ibaqa Beki</a>.
</p><p>He gave several of his high-status wives their own <i>ordos</i> or camps to live in and manage. Each camp also contained junior wives, concubines, and children. It was the job of the <a href="/wiki/Kheshig" title="Kheshig">Kheshig</a> (Mongol imperial guard) to protect the <a href="/wiki/Yurt" title="Yurt">yurts</a> of Temüjin's wives. The guards had to pay particular attention to the individual yurt and camp in which Temüjin slept, which could change every night as he visited different wives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBroadbridge201814,_74,_104_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBroadbridge201814,_74,_104-43">[40]</a></sup> When he set out on his military conquests, he usually took one wife with him and left the rest of his wives and concubines to manage the empire in his absence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBroadbridge201819–20_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBroadbridge201819–20-44">[41]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="Uniting_the_Mongol_confederations.2C_1184.E2.80.931206"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Uniting_the_Mongol_confederations,_1184–1206">Uniting the Mongol confederations, 1184–1206</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Rise_of_Genghis_Khan" title="Rise of Genghis Khan">Rise of Genghis Khan</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mongolia_XI.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="523" data-file-width="830" decoding="async" height="139" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Mongolia_XI.jpg/220px-Mongolia_XI.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Mongolia_XI.jpg/330px-Mongolia_XI.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Mongolia_XI.jpg/440px-Mongolia_XI.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mongolia_XI.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The locations of the Mongolian tribes during the Khitan <a href="/wiki/Liao_dynasty" title="Liao dynasty">Liao dynasty</a> (907–1125)</div></div></div>
<p>In the early 12th century, the Central Asian plateau north of China was divided into several prominent tribal <a href="/wiki/Confederation" title="Confederation">confederations</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Naimans" title="Naimans">Naimans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Merkit" title="Merkit">Merkits</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tatar" title="Tatar">Tatars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Khamag_Mongol" title="Khamag Mongol">Khamag Mongols</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Keraites" title="Keraites">Keraites</a>, that were often unfriendly towards each other, as evidenced by random raids, revenge attacks, and <a href="/wiki/Looting" title="Looting">plundering</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_attempts_at_power">Early attempts at power</span></h3>
<p>Temüjin began his ascent to power by offering himself as an ally (or, according to other sources, a <a href="/wiki/Vassal" title="Vassal">vassal</a>) to his father's <i>anda</i> (sworn brother or <a href="/wiki/Blood_brother" title="Blood brother">blood brother</a>) <a href="/wiki/Toghrul" title="Toghrul">Toghrul</a>, who was <a href="/wiki/Khan_(title)" title="Khan (title)">Khan</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Keraites" title="Keraites">Keraites</a>. This relationship was first reinforced when <a href="/wiki/B%C3%B6rte" title="Börte">Börte</a> was kidnapped by Merkits in around 1184. To win her back, Temüjin called on the support of Toghrul, who offered 20,000 of his Keraite warriors and suggested that Temüjin involve his childhood friend <a href="/wiki/Jamukha" title="Jamukha">Jamukha</a>, who was Khan of his own tribe, the Jadaran.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[42]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rift_with_Jamukha_and_defeat">Rift with Jamukha and defeat</span></h3>
<p>As <a href="/wiki/Jamukha" title="Jamukha">Jamukha</a> and Temüjin drifted apart in their friendship, each began consolidating power and they became rivals. Jamukha supported the traditional <a href="/wiki/Mongolian_nobility" title="Mongolian nobility">Mongolian aristocracy</a>, while Temüjin followed a <a href="/wiki/Meritocracy" title="Meritocracy">meritocratic</a> method, and attracted a broader range and lower class of followers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHildinger1997113_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHildinger1997113-46">[43]</a></sup> Following his earlier defeat of the Merkits, and a proclamation by the <a href="/wiki/Shamanism" title="Shamanism">shaman</a> <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Kokochu&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Kokochu (page does not exist)">Kokochu</a> that the <a href="/wiki/Tengrism" title="Tengrism">Eternal Blue Sky</a> had set aside the world for Temüjin, Temüjin began rising to power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHildinger1997114_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHildinger1997114-47">[44]</a></sup> In 1186, Temüjin was elected khan of the <a href="/wiki/Mongols" title="Mongols">Mongols</a>. Threatened by this rise, Jamukha attacked Temujin in 1187 with an army of 30,000 troops. Temüjin gathered his followers to defend against the attack, but was decisively beaten in the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Battle_of_Dalan_Balzhut&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Battle of Dalan Balzhut (page does not exist)">Battle of Dalan Balzhut</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHildinger1997114_47-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHildinger1997114-47">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELane2004xxvii_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELane2004xxvii-48">[45]</a></sup> However, Jamukha horrified and alienated potential followers by <a href="/wiki/Death_by_boiling" title="Death by boiling">boiling 70 young male captives alive</a> in cauldrons.<sup class="reference" id='cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeatherford2005[[Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_May_2020]]&lt;sup_class="noprint_Inline-Template_"_style="white-space:nowrap;"&gt;&amp;#91;&lt;i&gt;[[Wikipedia:Citing_sources|&lt;span_title="This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears.&amp;#32;(May_2020)"&gt;page&amp;nbsp;needed&lt;/span&gt;]]&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#93;&lt;/sup&gt;_49-0'><a href='#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeatherford2005[[Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_May_2020]]&lt;sup_class="noprint_Inline-Template_"_style="white-space:nowrap;"&gt;&amp;#91;&lt;i&gt;[[Wikipedia:Citing_sources|&lt;span_title="This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears.&amp;#32;(May_2020)"&gt;page&amp;nbsp;needed&lt;/span&gt;]]&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#93;&lt;/sup&gt;-49'>[46]</a></sup> Toghrul, as Temüjin's patron, was exiled to the <a href="/wiki/Qara_Khitai" title="Qara Khitai">Qara Khitai</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELane200423_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELane200423-50">[47]</a></sup> The life of Temüjin for the next 10 years is unclear, as historical records are mostly silent on that period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELane200423_50-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELane200423-50">[47]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Return_to_power">Return to power</span></h3>
<p>Around the year 1197, the <a href="/wiki/Jin_dynasty_(1115%E2%80%931234)" title="Jin dynasty (1115–1234)">Jin</a> initiated an attack against their formal vassal, the <a href="/wiki/Tatars" title="Tatars">Tatars</a>, with help from the <a href="/wiki/Keraites" title="Keraites">Keraites</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mongols" title="Mongols">Mongols</a>. Temüjin commanded part of this attack, and after victory, he and Toghrul were restored by the Jin to positions of power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELane200423_50-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELane200423-50">[47]</a></sup> The Jin bestowed Toghrul with the honorable title of Ong Khan, and Temüjin with a lesser title of <i>j'aut quri</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBiran201235_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBiran201235-51">[48]</a></sup>
</p><p>Around 1200, the main rivals of the <a href="/wiki/Khamag_Mongol" title="Khamag Mongol">Mongol confederation</a> (traditionally the "Mongols") were the <a href="/wiki/Naimans" title="Naimans">Naimans</a> to the west, the <a href="/wiki/Merkit" title="Merkit">Merkits</a> to the north, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tanguts" title="Tanguts">Tanguts</a> to the south, and the <a href="/wiki/Jin_dynasty_(1115%E2%80%931234)" title="Jin dynasty (1115–1234)">Jin</a> to the east.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Serven_Khaalga_Jurchen_inscription.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1170" data-file-width="1560" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Serven_Khaalga_Jurchen_inscription.jpg/220px-Serven_Khaalga_Jurchen_inscription.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Serven_Khaalga_Jurchen_inscription.jpg/330px-Serven_Khaalga_Jurchen_inscription.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Serven_Khaalga_Jurchen_inscription.jpg/440px-Serven_Khaalga_Jurchen_inscription.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Serven_Khaalga_Jurchen_inscription.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Jurchen_script" title="Jurchen script">Jurchen</a> inscription (1196) in Mongolia relating to Temüjin's alliance with the Jin against the Tatars</div></div></div>
<p>In his rule and his conquest of rival tribes, Temüjin broke with Mongol tradition in a few crucial ways. He delegated authority based on merit and loyalty, rather than family ties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeatherford200444_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeatherford200444-52">[49]</a></sup> As an incentive for absolute obedience and the <a href="/wiki/Yassa" title="Yassa">Yassa</a> code of law, Temüjin promised civilians and soldiers wealth from future war spoils. When he defeated rival tribes, he did not drive away their soldiers and abandon their civilians. Instead, he took the conquered tribe under his protection and integrated its members into his own tribe. He would even have his mother adopt orphans from the conquered tribe, bringing them into his family. These political innovations inspired great loyalty among the conquered people, making Temüjin stronger with each victory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeatherford200444_52-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeatherford200444-52">[49]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rift_with_Toghrul">Rift with Toghrul</span></h3>
<p><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Senggum&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Senggum (page does not exist)">Senggum</a>, son of Toghrul (Wang Khan), envied Temüjin's growing power and affinity with his father. He allegedly planned to assassinate Temüjin. Although Toghrul was allegedly saved on multiple occasions by Temüjin, he gave in to his son<sup class="reference" id='cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMan2007[[Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_May_2020]]&lt;sup_class="noprint_Inline-Template_"_style="white-space:nowrap;"&gt;&amp;#91;&lt;i&gt;[[Wikipedia:Citing_sources|&lt;span_title="This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears.&amp;#32;(May_2020)"&gt;page&amp;nbsp;needed&lt;/span&gt;]]&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#93;&lt;/sup&gt;_53-0'><a href='#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMan2007[[Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_May_2020]]&lt;sup_class="noprint_Inline-Template_"_style="white-space:nowrap;"&gt;&amp;#91;&lt;i&gt;[[Wikipedia:Citing_sources|&lt;span_title="This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears.&amp;#32;(May_2020)"&gt;page&amp;nbsp;needed&lt;/span&gt;]]&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#93;&lt;/sup&gt;-53'>[50]</a></sup> and became uncooperative with Temüjin. Temüjin learned of Senggum's intentions and eventually defeated him and his loyalists.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Djengiz_Kh%C3%A2n_et_Toghril_Ong_Khan.jpeg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="209" data-file-width="399" decoding="async" height="115" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Djengiz_Kh%C3%A2n_et_Toghril_Ong_Khan.jpeg/220px-Djengiz_Kh%C3%A2n_et_Toghril_Ong_Khan.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Djengiz_Kh%C3%A2n_et_Toghril_Ong_Khan.jpeg/330px-Djengiz_Kh%C3%A2n_et_Toghril_Ong_Khan.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/68/Djengiz_Kh%C3%A2n_et_Toghril_Ong_Khan.jpeg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Djengiz_Kh%C3%A2n_et_Toghril_Ong_Khan.jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Genghis Khan and Toghrul Khan, illustration from a 15th-century <a href="/wiki/Jami%27_al-tawarikh" title="Jami' al-tawarikh">Jami' al-tawarikh</a> manuscript</div></div></div>
<p>One of the later ruptures between Temüjin and Toghrul was Toghrul's refusal to give his daughter in marriage to <a href="/wiki/Jochi" title="Jochi">Jochi</a>, Temüjin's first son. This was disrespectful in Mongolian culture and led to a war. Toghrul allied with <a href="/wiki/Jamukha" title="Jamukha">Jamukha</a>, who already opposed Temüjin's forces. However, the dispute between Toghrul and Jamukha, plus the desertion of a number of their allies to Temüjin, led to Toghrul's defeat. Jamukha escaped during the conflict. This defeat was a catalyst for the fall and eventual dissolution of the <a href="/wiki/Keraites" title="Keraites">Keraite</a> tribe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAbbott2014362_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAbbott2014362-54">[51]</a></sup>
</p><p>After conquering his way steadily through the Alchi Tatars, Keraites, and Uhaz Merkits and acquiring at least one wife each time, Temüjin turned to the next threat on the steppe, the Turkic <a href="/wiki/Naimans" title="Naimans">Naimans</a> under the leadership of <a href="/wiki/Tayang_Khan" title="Tayang Khan">Tayang Khan</a> with whom Jamukha and his followers took refuge.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBroadbridge201889_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBroadbridge201889-55">[52]</a></sup> The Naimans did not surrender, although enough sectors again voluntarily sided with Temüjin.
</p><p>In 1201, a <a href="/wiki/Kurultai" title="Kurultai">Khuruldai</a> elected <a href="/wiki/Jamukha" title="Jamukha">Jamukha</a> as <a href="/wiki/Khan_(title)" title="Khan (title)">Gür Khan</a>, "universal ruler", a title used by the rulers of the <a href="/wiki/Qara_Khitai" title="Qara Khitai">Qara Khitai</a>. Jamukha's assumption of this title was the final breach with Temüjin, and Jamukha formed a coalition of tribes to oppose him. Before the conflict, several generals abandoned Jamukha, including <a href="/wiki/Subutai" title="Subutai">Subutai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jelme" title="Jelme">Jelme</a>'s well-known younger brother. After several battles, Jamukha was turned over to Temüjin by his own men in 1205.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>According to the <i>Secret History</i>, Temüjin again offered his friendship to <a href="/wiki/Jamukha" title="Jamukha">Jamukha</a>. Temüjin had killed the men who betrayed Jamukha, stating that he did not want disloyal men in his army. Jamukha refused the offer, saying that there can only be one sun in the sky, and he asked for a noble death. The custom was to die without spilling blood, specifically by having one's back broken. Jamukha requested this form of death, although he was known to have boiled his opponents' generals alive.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sole_ruler_of_the_Mongol_plains">Sole ruler of the Mongol plains</span></h3>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1097763485">.mw-parser-output .ambox{border:1px solid #a2a9b1;border-left:10px solid #36c;background-color:#fbfbfb;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .ambox+link+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+link+style+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+link+link+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+.mw-empty-elt+link+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+.mw-empty-elt+link+style+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+.mw-empty-elt+link+link+.ambox{margin-top:-1px}html body.mediawiki .mw-parser-output .ambox.mbox-small-left{margin:4px 1em 4px .ambox-delete{border-left:10px solid #b32424}.mw-parser-output .ambox-content{border-left:10px solid #f28500}.mw-parser-output .ambox-style{border-left:10px solid #fc3}.mw-parser-output ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">August 2022</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Genghis_Khan%27s_enthronement_in_1206.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="326" decoding="async" height="270" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Genghis_Khan%27s_enthronement_in_1206.jpg/220px-Genghis_Khan%27s_enthronement_in_1206.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/45/Genghis_Khan%27s_enthronement_in_1206.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Genghis_Khan%27s_enthronement_in_1206.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Genghis Khan proclaimed Khagan of all Mongols. Illustration from a 15th-century <a href="/wiki/Jami%27_al-tawarikh" title="Jami' al-tawarikh">Jami' al-tawarikh</a> manuscript.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mongol_Empire_c.1207.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="532" data-file-width="813" decoding="async" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Mongol_Empire_c.1207.png/220px-Mongol_Empire_c.1207.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Mongol_Empire_c.1207.png/330px-Mongol_Empire_c.1207.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Mongol_Empire_c.1207.png/440px-Mongol_Empire_c.1207.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mongol_Empire_c.1207.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mongol Empire <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr> 1207</div></div></div>
<p>The part of the <a href="/wiki/Merkit" title="Merkit">Merkit</a> clan that sided with the <a href="/wiki/Naimans" title="Naimans">Naimans</a> were defeated by <a href="/wiki/Subutai" title="Subutai">Subutai</a>, who was by then a member of Temüjin's personal guard and later became one of Temüjin's most successful <a href="/wiki/Commander" title="Commander">commanders</a>. The Naimans' defeat left Temüjin as the sole ruler of the <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_Steppe" title="Eurasian Steppe">Mongol steppe</a> – all the prominent confederations fell or united under his Mongol confederation.
</p><p>Accounts of Temüjin's life are marked by claims of a series of betrayals and conspiracies. These include rifts with his early allies such as Jamukha (who also wanted to be a ruler of Mongol tribes) and Wang Khan (his and his father's ally), his son <a href="/wiki/Jochi" title="Jochi">Jochi</a>, and problems with the most important <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shaman" title="Shaman">shaman</a>, who allegedly tried to drive a wedge between him and his loyal brother <a href="/wiki/Qasar" title="Qasar">Khasar</a>. His <a href="/wiki/Military_strategy" title="Military strategy">military strategies</a> showed a deep interest in gathering <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Intelligence_(information_gathering)" title="Intelligence (information gathering)">intelligence</a> and understanding the <a href="/wiki/Motivation" title="Motivation">motivations</a> of his rivals, exemplified by his extensive spy network and <a href="/wiki/Yam_(route)" title="Yam (route)">Yam</a> route systems. He seemed to be a quick student, adopting new technologies and ideas that he encountered, such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Siege_warfare" title="Siege warfare">siege warfare</a> from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_history_of_China_(pre-1911)" title="Military history of China (pre-1911)">Chinese</a>. He was also ruthless, demonstrated by his tactic of <a href="/wiki/Measuring_against_the_linchpin" title="Measuring against the linchpin">measuring against the linchpin</a>, used against the tribes led by Jamukha.
</p><p>As a result, by 1206, Temüjin had managed to unite or subdue the <a href="/wiki/Merkit" title="Merkit">Merkits</a>, <a href="/wiki/Naimans" title="Naimans">Naimans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mongols" title="Mongols">Mongols</a>, Keraites, <a href="/wiki/Tatars" title="Tatars">Tatars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uyghur_Khaganate#Successors" title="Uyghur Khaganate">Uyghurs</a>, and other disparate smaller tribes under his rule. This was a monumental feat. It resulted in peace between previously warring tribes, and a single political and military force. The union became known as the Mongols. At a <i><a href="/wiki/Kurultai" title="Kurultai">Khuruldai</a></i>, a council of Mongol chiefs, Temüjin was acknowledged as <a href="/wiki/Khan_(title)" title="Khan (title)">Khan</a> of the consolidated tribes and took the new title "Genghis Khan". The title <a href="/wiki/Khagan" title="Khagan">Khagan</a> was conferred posthumously by his son and successor Ögedei who took the title for himself (as he was also to be posthumously declared the founder of the <a href="/wiki/Yuan_dynasty" title="Yuan dynasty">Yuan dynasty</a>).
</p><p>
According to the Secret History of the Mongols, the chieftains of the conquered tribes pledged to Genghis Khan by proclaiming:</p><blockquote><p>"We will make you Khan; you shall ride at our head, against our foes. We will throw ourselves like lightning on your enemies. We will bring you their finest women and girls, their rich tents like palaces."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[54]</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<h2><span id="Military_campaigns.2C_1207.E2.80.931227"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Military_campaigns,_1207–1227">Military campaigns, 1207–1227</span></h2>
<div class="navbox-styles nomobile"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1061467846">.mw-parser-output .navbox{box-sizing:border-box;border:1px solid <ul><li><a href="/wiki/Rise_of_Genghis_Khan" title="Rise of Genghis Khan">Rise of Genghis Khan</a>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Chakirmaut" title="Battle of Chakirmaut">Chakirmaut</a></li></ul></li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Indus" title="Battle of the Indus">Indus</a></li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Kalka_River" title="Battle of the Kalka River">Kalka River</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasion_of_Volga_Bulgaria" title="Mongol invasion of Volga Bulgaria">Volga Bulgars</a></li></ul>
</div></td></tr></tbody></table></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasions_and_conquests" title="Mongol invasions and conquests">Mongol invasions and conquests</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Western_Xia_Dynasty">Western Xia Dynasty</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mongol_conquest_of_Western_Xia" title="Mongol conquest of Western Xia">Mongol conquest of Western Xia</a></div>
<p>During the 1206 political rise of Genghis Khan, the Mongol Empire created by Genghis Khan and his allies shared its western borders with the  of the <a href="/wiki/Tangut_people" title="Tangut people">Tangut</a> <a href="/wiki/Western_Xia" title="Western Xia">Western Xia</a> dynasty. To the east and south of the Western Xia dynasty was the militarily superior <a href="/wiki/Jin_dynasty_(1115%E2%80%931234)" title="Jin dynasty (1115–1234)">Jin dynasty</a>, founded by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manchu" title="Manchu">Manchurian</a> <a href="/wiki/Jurchen_people" title="Jurchen people">Jurchens</a>, who ruled northern China as well as being the traditional overlords of the Mongolian tribes for centuries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tim_may_1211_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-tim_may_1211-58">[55]</a></sup>
</p><p>Though militarily inferior to the neighboring Jin, the Western Xia still exerted a significant influence upon the adjacent northern <a href="/wiki/Steppe" title="Steppe">steppes</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tim_may_1211_58-1"><a href="#cite_note-tim_may_1211-58">[55]</a></sup> Following the death of the <a href="/wiki/Keraites" title="Keraites">Keraites</a> leader <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ong_Khan" title="Ong Khan">Ong Khan</a> to Temüjin's emerging <a href="/wiki/Mongol_Empire" title="Mongol Empire">Mongol Empire</a> in 1203, Keriat leader Nilqa Senggum led a small band of followers into Western Xia before later being expelled from Western Xia territory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tim_may_1211_58-2"><a href="#cite_note-tim_may_1211-58">[55]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bataille_entre_mongols_%26_chinois_(1211).jpeg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1181" data-file-width="1925" decoding="async" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Bataille_entre_mongols_%26_chinois_%281211%29.jpeg/220px-Bataille_entre_mongols_%26_chinois_%281211%29.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Bataille_entre_mongols_%26_chinois_%281211%29.jpeg/330px-Bataille_entre_mongols_%26_chinois_%281211%29.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Bataille_entre_mongols_%26_chinois_%281211%29.jpeg/440px-Bataille_entre_mongols_%26_chinois_%281211%29.jpeg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bataille_entre_mongols_%26_chinois_(1211).jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Battle between Mongol warriors and the <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">Chinese</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Si%C3%A8ge_de_Beijing_(1213-1214).jpeg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1181" data-file-width="1503" decoding="async" height="173" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Si%C3%A8ge_de_Beijing_%281213-1214%29.jpeg/220px-Si%C3%A8ge_de_Beijing_%281213-1214%29.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Si%C3%A8ge_de_Beijing_%281213-1214%29.jpeg/330px-Si%C3%A8ge_de_Beijing_%281213-1214%29.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Si%C3%A8ge_de_Beijing_%281213-1214%29.jpeg/440px-Si%C3%A8ge_de_Beijing_%281213-1214%29.jpeg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Si%C3%A8ge_de_Beijing_(1213-1214).jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Genghis Khan entering <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Using his rival Nilga Senggum's temporary refuge in Western Xia as a pretext, Temüjin launched a raid against the state in 1205 in the <a href="/wiki/Khara-Khoto" title="Khara-Khoto">Edsin</a> region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tim_may_1211_58-3"><a href="#cite_note-tim_may_1211-58">[55]</a></sup> The next year, in 1206, Temüjin was formally proclaimed Genghis Khan, ruler of all the Mongols, marking the official start of the Mongol Empire, and the same year <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Huanzong_of_Western_Xia" title="Emperor Huanzong of Western Xia">Emperor Huanzong</a> of the Western Xia was deposed by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Li_Anquan" title="Li Anquan">Li Anquan</a> in a <i>coup d'état</i>. In 1207, Genghis led another raid into Western Xia, invading the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ordos_Loop" title="Ordos Loop">Ordos region</a> and sacking <a href="/wiki/Wuhai" title="Wuhai">Wuhai</a>, the main garrison along the <a href="/wiki/Yellow_River" title="Yellow River">Yellow River</a>, before withdrawing in 1208. Genghis then began preparing for a full-scale invasion, organizing his people, army and state to first prepare for war.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[56]</a></sup>
</p><p>By invading Western Xia, Genghis Khan would gain a tribute-paying vassal, and also would take control of caravan routes along the <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road" title="Silk Road">Silk Road</a> and provide the Mongols with valuable revenue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kohn_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-kohn-60">[57]</a></sup> Furthermore, from Western Xia he could launch raids into the even more wealthy Jin dynasty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[58]</a></sup> He correctly believed that the more powerful young ruler of the Jin dynasty would not come to the aid of the Western Xia. When the Tanguts requested help from the Jin dynasty, they were refused.<sup class="reference" id='cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMan2007[[Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_May_2020]]&lt;sup_class="noprint_Inline-Template_"_style="white-space:nowrap;"&gt;&amp;#91;&lt;i&gt;[[Wikipedia:Citing_sources|&lt;span_title="This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears.&amp;#32;(May_2020)"&gt;page&amp;nbsp;needed&lt;/span&gt;]]&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#93;&lt;/sup&gt;_53-1'><a href='#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMan2007[[Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_May_2020]]&lt;sup_class="noprint_Inline-Template_"_style="white-space:nowrap;"&gt;&amp;#91;&lt;i&gt;[[Wikipedia:Citing_sources|&lt;span_title="This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears.&amp;#32;(May_2020)"&gt;page&amp;nbsp;needed&lt;/span&gt;]]&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#93;&lt;/sup&gt;-53'>[50]</a></sup> Despite initial difficulties in capturing Western Xia cities, Genghis Khan managed to force <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Renzong_of_Western_Xia" title="Emperor Renzong of Western Xia">Emperor Renzong</a> to submit to vassal status.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Jin_dynasty">Jin dynasty</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mongol_conquest_of_the_Jin_dynasty" title="Mongol conquest of the Jin dynasty">Mongol conquest of the Jin dynasty</a></div>
<p>In 1211, after the conquest of Western Xia, Genghis Khan planned again to conquer the <a href="/wiki/Jin_dynasty_(1115%E2%80%931234)" title="Jin dynasty (1115–1234)">Jin dynasty</a>. Luckily for the Mongols, Wanyan Jiujin, the field commander of the Jin army, made several tactical mistakes, including avoiding attacking the Mongols at the first opportunity using his overwhelming numerical superiority, and instead initially fortifying behind the Great wall. At the subsequent <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Yehuling" title="Battle of Yehuling">Battle of Yehuling</a>, which the Jin commander later committed to in the hope of using the mountainous terrain to his advantage against the Mongols, the general's emissary <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Shimo_Ming%27an&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Shimo Ming'an (page does not exist)">Ming'an</a> defected to the Mongol side and instead handed over intelligence on the movements of the Jin army, which was subsequently outmanoeuvred, resulting in hundreds of thousands of Jin casualties. So many, in fact, that decades later, when the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Daoism" title="Daoism">Daoist</a> sage <a href="/wiki/Qiu_Chuji" title="Qiu Chuji">Qiu Chuji</a> was passing through this pass to meet Genghis Khan, he was stunned to still see the bones of so many people scattered in the pass. On his way back, he camped close to this pass for three days and prayed for the departed souls. In 1215, Genghis besieged the Jin capital of Zhongdu (modern-day <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a>). According to <a href="/wiki/Ivar_Lissner" title="Ivar Lissner">Ivar Lissner</a>, the inhabitants resorted to firing gold and silver cannon shot on the Mongols with their muzzle-loading cannons when their supply of metal for ammunition ran out.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lissner_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lissner-62">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[61]</a></sup> The city was captured and sacked. This forced the Jin ruler, <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Xuanzong_of_Jin" title="Emperor Xuanzong of Jin">Emperor Xuanzong</a>, to move his capital south to <a href="/wiki/Kaifeng" title="Kaifeng">Kaifeng</a>, abandoning the northern half of his empire to the Mongols. Between 1232 and 1233, <a href="/wiki/Mongol_siege_of_Kaifeng" title="Mongol siege of Kaifeng">Kaifeng fell to the Mongols</a> under the reign of Genghis's third son and successor, Ögedei Khan. The Jin dynasty collapsed in 1234, after the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Caizhou" title="Siege of Caizhou">siege of Caizhou</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Qara_Khitai">Qara Khitai</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mongol_conquest_of_the_Qara_Khitai" title="Mongol conquest of the Qara Khitai">Mongol conquest of the Qara Khitai</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Kuchlug" title="Kuchlug">Kuchlug</a>, the deposed <a href="/wiki/Khan_(title)" title="Khan (title)">Khan</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Naimans" title="Naimans">Naiman</a> confederation that Genghis Khan defeated and folded into his Mongol Empire, fled west and usurped the <a href="/wiki/Khanate" title="Khanate">khanate</a> of <a href="/wiki/Qara_Khitai" title="Qara Khitai">Qara Khitai</a> (also known as the Western Liao, as it was originally established as remnants of the <a href="/wiki/Liao_dynasty" title="Liao dynasty">Liao dynasty</a>). Genghis Khan decided to conquer the Qara Khitai and defeat Kuchlug, possibly to take him out of power. By this time the Mongol army was exhausted from ten years of continuous campaigning in China against the Western Xia and Jin dynasty. Therefore, Genghis sent only two <a href="/wiki/Tumen_(unit)" title="Tumen (unit)"><i>tumen</i></a> (20,000 soldiers) against Kuchlug, under his younger general, <a href="/wiki/Jebe" title="Jebe">Jebe</a>, known as "The Arrow".
</p><p>With such a small force, the invading Mongols were forced to change strategies and resort to inciting internal revolt among Kuchlug's supporters, leaving the Qara Khitai more vulnerable to Mongol conquest. As a result, Kuchlug's army was defeated west of <a href="/wiki/Kashgar" title="Kashgar">Kashgar</a>. Kuchlug fled again, but was soon hunted down by Jebe's army and executed. By 1218, as a result of the defeat of Qara Khitai, the Mongol Empire and its control extended as far west as <a href="/wiki/Lake_Balkhash" title="Lake Balkhash">Lake Balkhash</a>, which bordered <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Khwarezmia" title="Khwarezmia"> Khwarazmia</a>, a Muslim state that reached the <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">Caspian Sea</a> to the west and <a href="/wiki/Persian_Gulf" title="Persian Gulf">Persian Gulf</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Sea" title="Arabian Sea">Arabian Sea</a> to the south.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[62]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Khwarazmian_Empire">Khwarazmian Empire</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mongol_conquest_of_Khwarezmia" title="Mongol conquest of Khwarezmia">Mongol conquest of Khwarezmia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Premongol.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="590" data-file-width="752" decoding="async" height="196" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Premongol.png/250px-Premongol.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Premongol.png/375px-Premongol.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Premongol.png/500px-Premongol.png 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Premongol.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Khwarazmian Empire (green) <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr> 1200, on the eve of the Mongol invasions</div></div></div>
<p>In the early 13th century, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Khwarazmian_dynasty" title="Khwarazmian dynasty">Khwarazmian dynasty</a> was governed by <a href="/wiki/Shah" title="Shah">Shah</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muhammad_II_of_Khwarezm" title="Muhammad II of Khwarezm">Ala ad-Din Muhammad</a>. Genghis Khan saw the potential advantage in Khwarazmia as a commercial trading partner using the <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road" title="Silk Road">Silk Road</a>, and he initially sent a 500-man <a href="/wiki/Camel_train" title="Camel train">caravan</a> to establish official trade ties with the empire. Genghis Khan and his family and commanders <a href="/wiki/Ortogh" title="Ortogh">invested</a> in the caravan gold, silver, silk, various kinds of textiles and fabrics and pelts to trade with the Muslim traders in the Khwarazmian lands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[63]</a></sup> However, <a href="/wiki/Inalchuq" title="Inalchuq">Inalchuq</a>, the governor of the Khwarazmian city of <a href="/wiki/Otrar" title="Otrar">Otrar</a>, attacked the caravan, claiming that the caravan contained spies and therefore was a conspiracy against Khwarazmia. The situation became further complicated because the governor later refused to make repayments for the looting of the caravans and hand over the perpetrators. Genghis Khan then sent a second group of three ambassadors (two Mongols and a Muslim) to meet the Shah himself, instead of the governor Inalchuq. The <a href="/wiki/Shah" title="Shah">Shah</a> had all the men shaved and the Muslim <a href="/wiki/Decapitation" title="Decapitation">beheaded</a> and sent his head back with the two remaining ambassadors. Outraged, Genghis Khan planned one of his largest invasion campaigns by organizing together around 100,000 soldiers (10 <a href="/wiki/Tumen_(unit)" title="Tumen (unit)">tumens</a>), his most capable generals and some of his sons. He left a commander and number of troops in China, designated his successors to be his family members and likely appointed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%C3%96gedei" title="Ögedei">Ögedei</a> to be his immediate successor and then went out to Khwarazmia.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:During_the_battle_of_Indus.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="837" data-file-width="600" decoding="async" height="307" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/During_the_battle_of_Indus.jpg/220px-During_the_battle_of_Indus.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/During_the_battle_of_Indus.jpg/330px-During_the_battle_of_Indus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/During_the_battle_of_Indus.jpg/440px-During_the_battle_of_Indus.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:During_the_battle_of_Indus.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Genghis Khan watches in amazement as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Khwarezm" title="Khwarezm">Khwarezmi</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jalal_ad-Din_Mingburnu" title="Jalal ad-Din Mingburnu">Jalal ad-Din</a> prepares to <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Indus" title="Battle of the Indus">ford the Indus</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The Mongol army under Genghis Khan, generals and his sons crossed the <a href="/wiki/Tian_Shan" title="Tian Shan">Tien Shan</a> mountains by entering the area controlled by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Khwarezmian_Empire" title="Khwarezmian Empire">Khwarazmian Empire</a>. After compiling intelligence from many sources Genghis Khan carefully prepared his army, which was divided into three groups. His son <a href="/wiki/Jochi" title="Jochi">Jochi</a> led the first division into the northeast of Khwarazmia. The second division under <a href="/wiki/Jebe" title="Jebe">Jebe</a> marched secretly to the southeast part of Khwarazmia to form, with the first division, a <a href="/wiki/Pincer_movement" title="Pincer movement">pincer attack</a> on <a href="/wiki/Samarkand" title="Samarkand">Samarkand</a>. The third division under Genghis Khan and <a href="/wiki/Tolui" title="Tolui">Tolui</a> marched to the northwest and attacked Khwarazmia from that direction.
</p><p>The Shah's army was split by diverse internecine feuds and by the Shah's decision to divide his army into small groups concentrated in various cities. This fragmentation was decisive in Khwarazmia's defeats, as it allowed the Mongols, although exhausted from the long journey, to immediately set about defeating small fractions of the Khwarazmian forces instead of facing a unified defense. The Mongol army quickly seized the town of <a href="/wiki/Otrar" title="Otrar">Otrar</a>, relying on superior strategy and tactics. Genghis Khan ordered the wholesale massacre of many of the civilians, enslaved the rest of the population and executed Inalchuq by pouring molten silver into his ears and eyes, as retribution for his actions.
</p><p>Next, Genghis Khan <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Bukhara" title="Siege of Bukhara">besieged the city of Bukhara</a>. <a href="/wiki/Bukhara" title="Bukhara">Bukhara</a> was not heavily fortified, with just a moat and a single wall, and the citadel typical of Khwarazmian cities. The city leaders opened the gates to the Mongols, though a unit of Turkish defenders held the city's citadel for another twelve days. The survivors from the citadel were executed, artisans and craftsmen were sent back to Mongolia, young men who had not fought were drafted into the Mongolian army and the rest of the population was sent into slavery.<sup class="reference" id='cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMorgan1986[[Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_May_2020]]&lt;sup_class="noprint_Inline-Template_"_style="white-space:nowrap;"&gt;&amp;#91;&lt;i&gt;[[Wikipedia:Citing_sources|&lt;span_title="This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears.&amp;#32;(May_2020)"&gt;page&amp;nbsp;needed&lt;/span&gt;]]&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#93;&lt;/sup&gt;_67-0'><a href='#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMorgan1986[[Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_May_2020]]&lt;sup_class="noprint_Inline-Template_"_style="white-space:nowrap;"&gt;&amp;#91;&lt;i&gt;[[Wikipedia:Citing_sources|&lt;span_title="This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears.&amp;#32;(May_2020)"&gt;page&amp;nbsp;needed&lt;/span&gt;]]&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#93;&lt;/sup&gt;-67'>[64]</a></sup> After the surrender of Bukhara, Genghis Khan also took the unprecedented step of personally entering the city, after which he had the city's aristocrats and elites brought to the mosque, where, through interpreters, he lectured them on their misdeeds, saying: "If you had not committed great sins, God would not have sent a punishment like me upon you."<sup class="reference" id='cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeatherford2005[[Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_August_2021]]&lt;sup_class="noprint_Inline-Template_"_style="white-space:nowrap;"&gt;&amp;#91;&lt;i&gt;[[Wikipedia:Citing_sources|&lt;span_title="This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears.&amp;#32;(August_2021)"&gt;page&amp;nbsp;needed&lt;/span&gt;]]&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#93;&lt;/sup&gt;_18-1'><a href='#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeatherford2005[[Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_August_2021]]&lt;sup_class="noprint_Inline-Template_"_style="white-space:nowrap;"&gt;&amp;#91;&lt;i&gt;[[Wikipedia:Citing_sources|&lt;span_title="This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears.&amp;#32;(August_2021)"&gt;page&amp;nbsp;needed&lt;/span&gt;]]&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#93;&lt;/sup&gt;-18'>[15]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Genghis_Khan_empire-en.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="658" data-file-width="1017" decoding="async" height="214" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Genghis_Khan_empire-en.svg/330px-Genghis_Khan_empire-en.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Genghis_Khan_empire-en.svg/495px-Genghis_Khan_empire-en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Genghis_Khan_empire-en.svg/660px-Genghis_Khan_empire-en.svg.png 2x" width="330"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Genghis_Khan_empire-en.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Significant conquests and movements of Genghis Khan and his generals</div></div></div>
<p>With the capture of Bukhara, the way was clear for the Mongols to advance on the capital of <a href="/wiki/Samarkand" title="Samarkand">Samarkand</a>, which possessed significantly better fortifications and a larger garrison compared to Bukhara. To overcome the city, the Mongols engaged in intensive psychological warfare, including the use of captured Khwarazmian prisoners as body shields. After several days only a few remaining soldiers, loyal supporters of the <a href="/wiki/Shah" title="Shah">Shah</a>, held out in the citadel. After the fortress fell, Genghis executed every soldier that had taken arms against him. According to the Persian historian <a href="/wiki/Ata-Malik_Juvayni" title="Ata-Malik Juvayni">Ata-Malik Juvayni</a>, the people of Samarkand were then ordered to evacuate and assemble in a plain outside the city, where they were killed and pyramids of severed heads raised as a symbol of victory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Juvayni_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-Juvayni-68">[65]</a></sup> Similarly, Juvayni wrote that in the city <a href="/wiki/Termez" title="Termez">Termez</a>, to the south of <a href="/wiki/Samarkand" title="Samarkand">Samarkand</a>, "all the people, both men and women, were driven out onto the plain, and divided in accordance with their usual custom, then they were all slain".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Juvayni_68-1"><a href="#cite_note-Juvayni-68">[65]</a></sup>
</p><p>Juvayni's account of mass killings at these sites is not corroborated by modern archaeology. Instead of killing local populations, the Mongols tended to enslave the conquered and either send them to Mongolia to act as menial labor or retain them for use in the war effort. The effect was still mass depopulation.<sup class="reference" id='cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeatherford2005[[Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_August_2021]]&lt;sup_class="noprint_Inline-Template_"_style="white-space:nowrap;"&gt;&amp;#91;&lt;i&gt;[[Wikipedia:Citing_sources|&lt;span_title="This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears.&amp;#32;(August_2021)"&gt;page&amp;nbsp;needed&lt;/span&gt;]]&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#93;&lt;/sup&gt;_18-2'><a href='#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeatherford2005[[Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_August_2021]]&lt;sup_class="noprint_Inline-Template_"_style="white-space:nowrap;"&gt;&amp;#91;&lt;i&gt;[[Wikipedia:Citing_sources|&lt;span_title="This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears.&amp;#32;(August_2021)"&gt;page&amp;nbsp;needed&lt;/span&gt;]]&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#93;&lt;/sup&gt;-18'>[15]</a></sup> The piling of a "pyramid of severed heads" happened not at <a href="/wiki/Samarkand" title="Samarkand">Samarkand</a> but at <a href="/wiki/Nishapur" title="Nishapur">Nishapur</a>, where Genghis Khan's son-in-law <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Toquchar&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Toquchar (page does not exist)">Toquchar</a> was killed by an arrow shot from the city walls after the residents revolted. The Khan then allowed his widowed daughter, who was pregnant at the time, to decide the fate of the city, and she decreed that the entire population be killed. She also supposedly ordered that every dog, cat and any other animals in the city by slaughtered, "so that no living thing would survive the murder of her husband".<sup class="reference" id='cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeatherford2005[[Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_August_2021]]&lt;sup_class="noprint_Inline-Template_"_style="white-space:nowrap;"&gt;&amp;#91;&lt;i&gt;[[Wikipedia:Citing_sources|&lt;span_title="This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears.&amp;#32;(August_2021)"&gt;page&amp;nbsp;needed&lt;/span&gt;]]&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#93;&lt;/sup&gt;_18-3'><a href='#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeatherford2005[[Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_August_2021]]&lt;sup_class="noprint_Inline-Template_"_style="white-space:nowrap;"&gt;&amp;#91;&lt;i&gt;[[Wikipedia:Citing_sources|&lt;span_title="This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears.&amp;#32;(August_2021)"&gt;page&amp;nbsp;needed&lt;/span&gt;]]&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#93;&lt;/sup&gt;-18'>[15]</a></sup> The sentence was duly carried out by the Khan's youngest son <a href="/wiki/Tolui" title="Tolui">Tolui</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nishapur_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-Nishapur-69">[66]</a></sup> According to widely circulated but unverified stories, the severed heads were then erected in separate piles for the men, women and children.<sup class="reference" id='cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeatherford2005[[Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_August_2021]]&lt;sup_class="noprint_Inline-Template_"_style="white-space:nowrap;"&gt;&amp;#91;&lt;i&gt;[[Wikipedia:Citing_sources|&lt;span_title="This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears.&amp;#32;(August_2021)"&gt;page&amp;nbsp;needed&lt;/span&gt;]]&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#93;&lt;/sup&gt;_18-4'><a href='#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeatherford2005[[Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_August_2021]]&lt;sup_class="noprint_Inline-Template_"_style="white-space:nowrap;"&gt;&amp;#91;&lt;i&gt;[[Wikipedia:Citing_sources|&lt;span_title="This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears.&amp;#32;(August_2021)"&gt;page&amp;nbsp;needed&lt;/span&gt;]]&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#93;&lt;/sup&gt;-18'>[15]</a></sup>
